                      <div data-reactid="664">
                       This house is a large Craftsman home, an LA classic built in 1909! This bedroom for guests faces the large back yard and has two big windows, and light colored real wood floors, real bed, desk with office chair. Very centrally located, close to downtown LA and USC, 10 and 110 Fwys. Large backyard with fruit trees and patio furniture to enjoy the sunny LA weather. Free parking right in front of the house; equipped with washer, dryer and dishwasher.
                      </div>
                      <div data-reactid="665">
                       This is a classic four bedroom LA Craftsman home shared with the host, co-host, Marley the Bosnian cat, Jack the small American dog, and potentially another Airbnb guest. It has housed people from all over the world for over a decade, both for long term and short stays (more reviews on CS as VONVON). There is ample free street parking. Large back yard with lemon, avocado and apple trees, and big front yard. The house is big, 1600 sq ft, with large living room that includes flatscreen with Hulu and Netflix, dining room with large table and spacious fully equipped kitchen - so no feeling cramped. The bedroom is small but cozy, sleeps one in a comfy twin size bed. It has a desk/vanity and chair, two mirrors, and a rack to hang clothes with hangers provided. It has light colored real wood floors, two big windows overlooking the large back yard, a night stand, clean towels, blow dryer and snacks. Help yourself to tea and coffee in the kitchen. For those who may have mobility issues, the house is a single story but there are 4 steps up to the porch and also down into the back yard.
                      </div>
                      <div data-reactid="666">
                       This is the 'hood you have heard about in rap songs. Is it scary? Naaah - come check it out for yourself. We are on a nice family street shared with an elementary school (ice cream trucks are the bonus amenity!) The neighborhood has just been proposed to be officially declared by the LA City Planning Department a "Los Angeles Character Neighborhood" ('cause we have character!) A film crew favorite.... Very close to the museum complex - California Science Center, Natural History Museum, African American Museum - and also to University of Southern California, the LA Coliseum and LA Sports Arena. Staples Center/LA Live and the LA Convention Center is an 8 dollar Uber ride away (parking there for 3 hrs costs $25!) Very centrally located and easy freeway and public transit access so you can visit all major LA sites including the beach without spending hours in traffic. Please read the neighborhood description including pics provided by airbnb by the map. If this is not the location you had in mind, please search for Beverly Hills, Hollywood, Santa Monica or whatever other city you are really interested in. Los Angeles is a huge place so if it's your first time to visit, do searches of distances between sights in the greater Los Angeles area to get a realistic idea of how much time you will need to get around to really see all you want to see, especially if you will be using public transport only. You might want to consider staying for a shorter time in different areas or renting a car to get around like most Angelinos. We want guests who are happy to come to our vibrant neighborhood and are realistic in their expectations of Los Angeles. Thank you!

                       An exciting adventure awaits at the Cimarron House, home of L.A.’s best shared housing. We are family owned and operated. In this home away from home, you’ll have access to daily free hot breakfast, convenient public transportation, freeway access, free high speed Internet and laundry. We are also in close proximity to Venice Beach, USC, and Hollywood. The Cimarron House is perfect for solo travelers, business travelers and groups. Come explore all that Los Angeles has to offer.

                      <div data-reactid="867">
                       The house is attached to a historic Hollywood mansion, originally built by iconic African-American actor Eddie "Rochester" Anderson. There is a furnished kitchen and dining area, living room, free laundry machines, and a large backyard with swimming pool and outdoor tables. Free wifi is available throughout the property.
                      </div>
                      <div data-reactid="868">
                       In mid-city Los Angeles, a mere ten minutes from USC, our properties are centrally located in the heart of the city (6 miles from Hollywood and Downtown LA, 12 miles from the beach.) The closest Metro stop is a 10-minute walk, and will take you directly to Santa Monica, downtown, and other popular tourist destinations. We are just 3 miles from Culver City, with its many dining options, parks and hiking trails, farmer's markets, and galleries.

                       <li data-reactid="878"><p data-reactid="879">The only problem with my stay: There was a robbery in the neighborhood and the police sealed off the area, so I had to walk through L.A. alone from 11pm - 5am (with $3,000 in cash on me). Obviously this isn't the fault of Eddie or any of the hostel staff. It is Amerikkka's fault. Bring a revolver if you come to the USA. With that said all the people staying and working at the hostel were interesting and cool. I think there are some longer-term residents here (I used to live long-term in a hostel in Alaska myself) and they look out for the visitors, they know L.A. and I had many great conversations and spliffs with a variety of ladies and gentlemen. I spent most of my time out and about. The local train goes direct to Santa Monica &amp; Downtown. A weekly pass is $25, but be careful because this is the USA, not a civilized country, and the trains do NOT run 24/7. However the buses will take you very far during the day, all the way to Zuma Beach, which I highly recommend... If you've ever listened to a classic 2Pac album, the imagery of L.A. is alive here. The weight bench in the backyard is a nice touch of local color. The pool is clean, they have a big screen for movies, you can smoke outside, etc. As far as I could tell there are no good local bars, or even grocery stores in the area... Then again L.A. is notorious for being car-oriented and I'm used to living in Europe and Asia where you can walk to get whatever you need... One morning I woke up and Fergie walked out of the bathroom and gave me a massage. Kidding :-) I didn't see any famous people, but I did visit a lot of famous sites, including the grave of Mr. Harry Nilsson (in Thousand Oaks, a long but beautiful bus ride). In short if you're staying in L.A. and need a well-located place, easy access to downtown, the beaches, the airport, and don't mind the hostel lifestyle this is a great option... The atmosphere inside the mansion is very old-school 'if these walls could talk' style and I only wish I had known more of the history...                       <div data-reactid="1620">
                       <li data-reactid="1621"><p data-reactid="1622">I had to stay here for work and it was perfect for me. It was within walking distance to the USC campus (which Camp Flog Gnaw was held this year) and the neighborhood wasn't too hard to navigate. I enjoyed taking in the sights!</p><span data-reactid="1623">Eric</span><span data-reactid="1624">2016-11-14T00:00:00Z</span></li>
                       <li data-reactid="1625"><p data-reactid="1626">Elisabeth is a pleasant host and was helpful in many ways. The neighborhood is quiet and people are nice. The house has a cozy backyard and there is cleaning few times a week on shared spaces in the house. However, the room is slightly dark and could be tiring for long-term stay. Both the rooms and the house have password locks, so it is very safe and private. There are new people moving in all the time, so it's a good place to meet people with different backgrounds. Location is okay; very close to downtown (ride a bike or use Uber), but it is far from other central/touristic places. I highly recommend renting a car to get around. Overall, I had a good experience and I recommend staying with Elisabeth, especially for short-term stay. </p><span data-reactid="1627">Burak</span><span data-reactid="1628">2014-07-14T00:00:00Z</span></li>
                       <li data-reactid="1629"><p data-reactid="1630">Good</p><span data-reactid="1631">凌飞</span><span data-reactid="1632">2016-08-20T00:00:00Z</span></li>
                       <li data-reactid="1633"><p data-reactid="1634">Totally awesome place to stay at a reasonable price. You probably won't find better long term accommodations in LA.</p><span data-reactid="1635">Rudy</span><span data-reactid="1636">2014-12-01T00:00:00Z</span></li>
                       <li data-reactid="1637"><p data-reactid="1638">Elisabeth was gracious and helpful. The neighborhood, close to USC, was one/two blocks off of the majors streets. So, it was relatively quiet, yet readily accessible. Wifi was somewhat dicey, no doubt due to high student usage.                        <li data-reactid="2128"><p data-reactid="2129">I stayed here for spring break with four other girls; the room was fine, and Brian was nice enough, but this listing was completely misleading and made for a very uncomfortable stay. First of all, the area is very sketchy, and not at all "close to the beach and culture" as the listing claims. If you have a car it's not so bad, but there isn't any near by public transportation, so if you're looking to explore LA on a low budget, I wouldn't recommend. It says there is free parking, but the lot is incredibly tight with tall pillars blocking many of the spaces. I saw another review mention she scraped the side of her car, and we easily could have done the same. So be aware of that, and unless you are an incredibly skilled driver, I would not recommend parking in the lot. There is street parking, but the neighborhood is sketchy and I personally did not feel comfortable walking around, so be aware of that as well. Even though the listing says it's a private room, Brian did not mention that there would be other guests there as well. We had a group of 5, and assumed it would but just us and Brian, but we quickly found out there were other guests. Originally when I asked Brian who else was staying there he told me a couple and 2 guys in the room next to us, but we eventually found out the group of guys was 4, and the "couple" was a family. This left 11 people sharing one small bathroom, and of course the hot water was awful. Brian said he had another bathroom but it was broken, but we thought we heard running water upstairs also, which led us (and also the other guests staying there) to believe he was lying and that he was keeping a private bathroom for himself. As for amenities, we had access to the kitchen, and the wifi was slow, but not too bad. But the "air-conditioning" was just a fan, and when we asked for extra towels, blankets, and pillows, he said he didn't have more. We ended up sharing 2 towels between the 5 of us, and I had to sleep on the floor with no pillows. All of that being said, the place was cheap and clean, and Brian was easy to contact. If you are looking for a quick place in LA to crash, it may work for you, as long as you're aware of the area you're in. But if you are a group with a longer stay and looking for a comfortable place after a long day of explore the city, I would suggest spending a bit more money for something less stressful.</p><span data-reactid="2130">Geneva </span><span data-reactid="2131">2017-03-22T00:00:00Z</span></li>
